- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls

# LLVM Optimization Pass Pipeline Propagation

## Your Task

Trace how an LLVM optimization pass is registered in the pass pipeline and executed. Find all C++ source files in `llvm/llvm-project` that participate in the optimization pipeline lifecycle: 1. The file that defines the `PassBuilder` class and its method for building the default O2 optimization pipeline (look in `llvm/lib/Passes/`). 2. The file that defines the `PassManager` template class — the core pass execution engine (look in `llvm/include/llvm/IR/`). 3. The file that implements `PassBuilderPipelines` which assembles the default module/function simplification pipelines. 4. The file that registers all standard passes via `PassRegistry.def`. 5. For a concrete example, the file implementing `DeadStoreElimination` in `llvm/lib/Transforms/Scalar/`. Report the repo, file path, and key class or function name for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `github.com/llvm/llvm-project` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `github.com/gcc-mirror/gcc` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

{"content":"1: //===- DeadStoreElimination.cpp - MemorySSA Backed Dead Store Elimination -===//\n2: //\n3: // Part of the LLVM Project, under the Apache License v2.0 with LLVM Exceptions.\n4: // See https://llvm.org/LICENSE.txt for license information.\n5: // SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 WITH LLVM-exception\n6: //\n7: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n8: //\n9: // The code below implements dead store elimination using MemorySSA. It uses\n10: // the following general approach: given a MemoryDef, walk upwards to find\n11: // clobbering MemoryDefs that may be killed by the starting def. Then check\n12: // that there are no uses that may read the location of the original MemoryDef\n13: // in between both MemoryDefs. A bit more concretely:\n14: //\n15: // For all MemoryDefs StartDef:\n16: // 1. Get the next dominating clobbering MemoryDef (MaybeDeadAccess) by walking\n17: //    upwards.\n18: // 2. Check that there are no reads between MaybeDeadAccess and the StartDef by\n19: //    checking all uses starting at MaybeDeadAccess and walking until we see\n20: //    StartDef.\n21: // 3. For each found CurrentDef, check that:\n22: //   1. There are no barrier instructions between CurrentDef and StartDef (like\n23: //       throws or stores with ordering constraints).\n24: //   2. StartDef is executed whenever CurrentDef is executed.\n25: //   3. StartDef completely overwrites CurrentDef.\n26: // 4. Erase CurrentDef from the function and MemorySSA.\n27: //\n28: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n29: \n30: #include \"llvm/Transforms/Scalar/DeadStoreElimination.h\"\n31: #include \"llvm/ADT/APInt.h\"\n32: #include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n33: #include \"llvm/ADT/MapVector.h\"\n34: #in

Perfect! I've successfully traced the LLVM optimization pass pipeline and created the answer file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've located and documented **5 key C++ source files** in the LLVM project that participate in the optimization pipeline lifecycle:

1. **PassBuilder** (`llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilder.cpp`): The orchestrator class containing `buildModuleOptimizationPipeline()` method that constructs the O2 optimization pipeline

2. **PassManager** (`llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h`): The core template class that executes the pipeline with its `run()` method

3. **PassBuilderPipelines** (`llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilderPipelines.cpp`): Contains the implementation of the module/function simplification pipeline assembly logic

4. **PassRegistry** (`llvm/lib/Passes/PassRegistry.def`): A macro-based registry file that registers all standard optimization and analysis passes

5. **DeadStoreElimination** (`llvm/lib/Transforms/Scalar/DeadStoreElimination.cpp`): Concrete example showing how an individual pass (DSEPass) is implemented

The execution chain flows as: **PassBuilder::buildModuleOptimizationPipeline()** → **PassRegistry.def** (for pass lookup) → **PassManager::run()** → individual passes like **DSEPass::run()**

The complete findings are in `/workspace/answer.json` with file paths, symbols, execution chain, and a detailed narrative explanation.

partially overwritten by the store to 'Loc'\n776:     //   b) the killing store is fully contained in the dead one and\n777:     //   c) they both have a constant value\n778:     //   d) none of the two stores need padding\n779:     // Merge the two stores, replacing the dead store's value with a\n780:     // merge of both values.\n781:     // TODO: Deal with other constant types (vectors, etc), and probably\n782:     // some mem intrinsics (if needed)\n783: \n784:     APInt DeadValue = cast<ConstantInt>(DeadI->getValueOperand())->getValue();\n785:     APInt KillingValue =\n786:         cast<ConstantInt>(KillingI->getValueOperand())->getValue();\n787:     unsigned KillingBits = KillingValue.getBitWidth();\n788:     assert(DeadValue.getBitWidth() > KillingValue.getBitWidth());\n789:     KillingValue = KillingValue.zext(DeadValue.getBitWidth());\n790: \n791:     // Offset of the smaller store inside the larger store\n792:     unsigned BitOffsetDiff = (KillingOffset - DeadOffset) * 8;\n793:     unsigned LShiftAmount =\n794:         DL.isBigEndian() ? DeadValue.getBitWidth() - BitOffsetDiff - KillingBits\n795:                          : BitOffsetDiff;\n796:     APInt Mask = APInt::getBitsSet(DeadValue.getBitWidth(), LShiftAmount,\n797:                                    LShiftAmount + KillingBits);\n798:     // Clear the bits we'll be replacing, then OR with the smaller\n799:     // store, shifted appropriately.\n800:     APInt Merged = (DeadValue & ~Mask) | (KillingValue << LShiftAmount);\n801: ",

PassBuilder class is the main orchestrator of pass construction. Analyses are registered with `MODULE_ANALYSIS` macros, transformation passes with `MODULE_PASS`, `FUNCTION_PASS`, etc. The PassBuilder includes this file multiple times to extract pass metadata for parsing and instantiation.\\n\\n5. **DeadStoreElimination Concrete Example** (`llvm/lib/Transforms/Scalar/DeadStoreElimination.cpp` and header `llvm/include/llvm/Transforms/Scalar/DeadStoreElimination.h`): The `DSEPass` class (defined in the header) implements the actual dead store elimination optimization. It contains the `run(Function &F, FunctionAnalysisManager &FAM)` method that executes the pass over a function, using MemorySSA and alias analysis to identify and eliminate redundant store instructions.\\n\\nThe pipeline execution flow is: PassBuilder::buildModuleOptimizationPipeline() \u2192 PassRegistry.def (for pass lookup) \u2192 PassManager::run() \u2192 individual passes like DSEPass::run()\"\n}\n",
